convict [kən’vɪkt]

释义 • v. to declare in a lawcourt that sb. is guilty (of a crime) 证明……有罪，宣判……有罪 n. a person who has been convicted of crime and is being punished, esp. by imprisonment 已决犯

联想 • con(共同 )+vict(im)(受害者 )→当你犯罪被捕后 ，你和被害人实际上都为受害者 。

搭配 • convict sb. of sth. 因为某事宣判某人有罪

派生 • convicted adj. 定罪的

conviction4 n. 定罪 ，判罪 ；坚定的信念 ，信仰 ；深信 ，确信

例句 • Children who persistently bully are more likely to grow up to be physically violent, and convicted of anti-social offences. (IELTS6,T4,R3)一直欺凌他人的小孩长大后更可能有暴力倾向 ，更容易犯下反社会的罪行 。

cookery [’kʊkərɪ]

释义 • n. the art and practice of cooking 烹调法

词根 • cook+ery(法 )→烹调法

派生 • cooker n. 做饭的器具

cook n. 厨师

例句 • I’ m taking a month’ s cookery course at a local college. (IELTS3,TB,R2)我在当地的大学学习了一个月的烹饪课程 。

cooperation [kəʊˌɒpə’reɪʃən]

释义 • n. the act or practice of cooperating 合作，协作，协助，配合

词根 • co(共同 )+oper(工作 )+ation(做 )→一起做工作 →合作 ，协作

派生 • cooperate1 v. 合作 ，协作

cooperative2 adj. 乐意合作的 ，合作的 ，合作性的 n. 合作企业 ，合作社

例句 • Thank you for your cooperation ! (IELTS5,TB,W1)谢谢你的合作 ！

cornerstone [’kɔːnəstəʊn]

释义 • n. a stone at the corner of a building uniting two intersecting walls; a quoin. 墙角石 ；such a stone, often inscribed, laid at a ceremony marking the origin of a building 奠基石

词根 • corner+stone→墙角的石头 →奠基石

例句 • It is the cornerstone of Standard English, an achievement which, in James Boswell ’ s words, conferred stability on the language of his country. (IELTS5,T1,R1) 这一成就是标准英语的奠基石 。 用 James Boswell 的话说 ， 这为其国家语言的稳定性奠定了基础 。

corps [kɔː]

释义 • n. a military force made up of two or more divisions 部队，兵种

词根 • corp(团体 )+s→团队 →部队

例句 • The leaders had built up a corps of racketeers and used rockets successfully against the British in the late eighteenth century. (IELTS3,T1,R1)这些领导人组建了火箭部队 ，并在 18世纪末成功地用火箭打败了英国人 。

correlation [ˌkɒrə’leɪʃən]

释义 • n. a causal, complementary, parallel, or reciprocal relationship, especially a structural, functional, or qualitative correspondence between two comparable entities 相关，相关性

词根 • cor(共同 )+relation(关系 )→共同的关系 →相关

例句 • One interesting correlation Manton uncovered is that better-educated people are likely to live longer. (IELTS6,T2,R2) Manton发现了一个有趣的关联现象 ，那就是 ：受到良好教育的人可能活得更长 。

cortical [’kɔːtɪkəl]

释义 • adj. of, relating to, derived from, or consisting of cortex (大脑)皮质的，皮层的

派生 • cortex5 n. (大脑 )皮层

例句 • In laboratory simulations of challenging activities such as driving, those who felt in control of their lives pumped out lower levels of stress hormones such as cortical . (IELTS6,T2,R2)在实验室模拟富有挑战性的活动时 ，如开车 ，那些认为能够控制自己生活的人产生较低水平的压力荷尔蒙 ，如皮层荷尔蒙 。

costume [ˈkɒstju:m]

释义 • n . a set of clothes in a style typical of a particular country or historical period戏装，演出服

例句 • We’ re also considering hiring out costumes to amateur drama clubs. (IELTS11,T2, L2) 我们正在考虑将戏服出租给业余的戏剧团。

counterproductive [’kaʊntəprəˌdʌktɪv]

释义 • adj. tending to hinder rather than serve one’ s purpose 适得其反的

词根 • counter(against)+productive(多产的 )→适得其反的

例句 • This phenomenon can be partly attributed to the common counterproductive approach to study (making extreme efforts to memorise, tensing muscles, inducing fatigue), but it also simply reflects the way the brain functions. (IELTS7,T1,R3)这种现象可以部分归因于经常起相反作用的学习方式 (极度努力记忆 、肌肉紧张 、导致疲劳 )，但这也简单地表明了大脑的工作方式 。

courtship [’kɔːtʃɪp]

释义 • n. the act, process, or period of courting 求爱期，恋爱期；(动物的)求偶

派生 • court v. 讨好 ，向 ……献殷勤 ；和 ……谈恋爱

courtesy n. 礼貌 ，谦恭有礼

courteous adj. 谦恭的 ，有礼貌的

例句 • This contact may help to maintain order within a group, and stroking or touching are part of the courtship ritual in most species. (IELTS4,T1,R2)这种接触可以帮助维持群内秩序 ，抚摩和接触对很多物种来说是求偶仪式的一部分 。

craze [kreɪz]

释义 • n. enthusiastic, usu. brief, interest in sth. 风靡一时的事物，狂热

派生 • crazy1 adj. 疯狂的

例句 • Almost overnight movies became a craze , and by 1905 people in America were lining up to see movies in “store theatres” , as they were called then. (IELTS6,T2,L4)几乎在一夜之间 ，电影开始盛行 。而到 1905年 ，美国人排队买票去他们所谓的 “商店剧院”看电影 。

credibility [ˌkredə’bɪlɪtɪ]

释义 • n. the quality, capability, or power to elicit belief 可靠性，可信性，可信度

词根 • cred(相信 )+ibility(可能性 )→可信性

派生 • credit30 n. 信任 ；信用 ，信贷 v. 记入贷方 ，把 ……归于

credible1 adj. 可信的 ，可靠的

creditable adj. 值得表扬的 ，令人钦佩的

credence1 n. 信用 ；信任 ；凭证

例句 • But in recent years IQ has had much more credibility and weight. (IELTS6,T2,R3) 但是近些年 ，智商拥有更多的可信性和重要性 。

crude [kruːd]

释义 • adj. in the natural state; unrefined 天然的，粗糙的 ；not well finished; not completely worked out; rough 粗俗的

词根 • c+rud(天然的 ，粗糙的 )+e→天然的 ，粗糙的

例句 • Other than bows, arrows and crude digging sticks, the only tools the Siriono seemed to possess were two machetes worn to the size of pocket-knives. (IELTS3,T3,R2)除了弓 、箭和粗糙的挖掘棍 ，Siriono拥有的唯一工具是两个砍刀 ，它们被磨成口袋刀的尺寸 。

cruel [’kruːəl]

释义 • adj. making others suffer, esp. intentionally 残忍的，残酷的，残暴的

联想 • 发音记忆 ：“刻肉”→残忍的

派生 • cruelty n. 残忍 ，残酷 ；暴行 ，虐待

例句 • The anthropologist concluded that the tribesmen were unusually aggressive and cruel . (IELTS3,T3,R2)人类学家得出结论 ，这个部落的人无比凶残 、侵略成性 。

crystalline [’krɪstəlaɪn]

释义 • adj. made of or resembling crystals 含水晶的，晶状的

派生 • crystal14 n. 水晶 ，结晶体

crystallize v. 使结晶 ，使晶化 ；使明确化

例句 • Are the rocks heavy, with huge crystalline basalt shapes, like the Giants Causeway in Northern Ireland? (IELTS4,T3,R2)那些重的 、有巨大的结晶质的玄武岩和北爱尔兰的巨人之路上的石头一样吗 ？

curb [kɜ:b]

释义 • v. to control or limit sth; restrain; check 制止 ，束缚

同义 • restrain, restrict, control, limit

例句 • In the short term it might curb the growth in road transport through the better loading ratio of goods vehicles and occupancy rates of passenger vehicles expected as a result of the increase in the price of transport. (IELTS10,T1,R2)短期来看 ，通过提高运输费从而提高货运车辆的承载率和载客车辆的上座率 ，公路运输的增长会受到限制 。

curly [’kɜːlɪ]

释义 • adj. curling; full of curls 卷曲的，波浪式的

派生 • curl v. 使卷曲

例句 • He’ ll grow up to be with masses of curly black hair. (IELTS3,T4,L1)他长大后会长出很多卷曲的黑头发 。

curtail [kɜː’teɪl]

释义 • v. to make (sth.) shorter or less; to reduce 减少，削减，限制

派生 • curtailment n. 减少 ，削减 ，限制

例句 • While the Inuit may not actually starve if hunting and trapping are curtailed by climate change, there has certainly been an impact on people’ s health. (IELTS6,T1,R3)虽然 如果气候变化造成捕猎和诱捕受限 ， 因纽特人不会真的挨饿 ， 但是他们的健康肯定会受影响 。

cyclist [’saɪklɪst]

释义 • n. a person who rides a bicycle 骑自行车的人

词根 • cycl(e)(自行车 )+ist(人 )→骑自行车的人

例句 • A lot of their work comes down to measurement—everything from the exact angle of a swimmer’ s dive to the second-by-second power output of a cyclist . (IELTS6,T1,R1)他们的很多工作归根到底就是测量 ——从游泳者跳水的准确角度到自行车手每秒钟的力量输出的测量 。

daunted [dɔːnt ɪ d]

释义 • adj. afraid 畏惧的，胆怯的

派生 • daunt v. 使胆怯 ，使畏缩

dauntless adj. 无所畏惧的 ，勇敢的

例句 • Now, the Semira Mountains are among the highest in the world but you mustn’ t be too daunted , we will mainly be trekking in the foothills only, although there will be spectacular views even in the foothills. (IELTS7,T3,L2) Semira 山是世界上最高的山峰之一 ，但不要害怕 ，我们主要是在山脚下游览 ，山脚下也有很多壮丽的景观 。

dearth [dɜːθ]

释义 • n. shortage; scarcity 缺乏，不足

联想 • d+earth→地球资源总有一天会缺乏的 →缺乏

搭配 • dearth of 缺乏 ，不足

同义 • lack, deficiency

例句 • Typically, children do not end up on the streets due to a single cause, but to a combination of factors: a dearth of adequately funded schools, the demand for income at home, family breakdown and violence. (IELTS4,T3,R1)通常情况下 ，孩子流浪街头的原因不止一个 ，而是许多因素共同作用的结果 ：学校经费短缺 、家庭收入不足 、家庭解体和家庭暴力 。

decay [dɪ’keɪ]

释义 • v. (cause sth. to) become bad; to rot; to decompose 腐烂，腐败 n. (state reached by the process of) decaying 腐烂，腐败，破损

联想 • decay—decade，事物在十几年后肯定都腐烂了 →腐烂 ，腐败

例句 • Archaeological traces of far more elaborate cultures have been dismissed as the ruins of invaders from outside the region, abandoned to decay in the uncompromising tropical environment. (IELTS3,T3,R2)更加复杂的文化中的考古学遗迹由于外界侵略者的入侵而变成废墟 ，它们被遗弃在恶劣的热带环境中自生自灭 。

deception [dɪ’sepʃən]

释义 • n. deceiving or being deceived 欺骗，欺骗行为

词根 • 已知 receive的名词形式为 reception，可以推出 deception动词为 deceive，de(变坏 )+ceive(拿 ，抓 )→用不好的手段拿 →欺骗

派生 • deceive v. 欺骗

deceptive2 adj. 骗人的 ，靠不住的 ；虚假的

deceptively1 adv. 造成假象地

例句 • Now small amounts like this may seem insignificant for individual customers—too small to worry about—but for the company this deception might result in massive illegal profit. (IELTS4,T2,L4)这么小的数额对单个顾客来讲是微不足道的 ——太小了 ，以致顾客不会在意 ——但是对于这么大的公司来说 ，这种欺骗可能带来巨大的非法盈利 。

decipher [dɪˈsaɪfə(r)]

释义 • v . convert (a text written in code, or a coded signal) into normal language 解读；破译（密码）

词根 • de-（去掉）+cipher（暗号）→去掉暗号→译解

例句 • The harder it is to decipher the meaning, the more rewarding is the moment of recognition. (IELTS11,T2, R3) 意义越是难以被解读，破解之后就越有一种成就感。

decompose [ˌdiːkəm’pəʊz]

释义 • v. to become bad or rotten; decay 腐烂，腐败 ；to separate (a substance, light, etc.) into its parts 分解

词根 • de(否定 ，非 ，相反 )+compose(组合 )→跟组合相反 →分解 ；腐败

派生 • decomposition n. 分解 ；腐烂 ，腐败

例句 • The digested dung in these burrows is an excellent food supply for the earthworms, which decompose it further to provide essential soil nutrients. (IELTS3,T2,R1)在洞穴中被消化的动物粪便是蚯蚓极佳的食物来源 ，它们将这些粪便进一步分解 ，为土壤提供重要的肥料 。

decrepit [dɪ’krepɪt]

释义 • adj. made weak by age or hard use 破旧的，衰老的

词根 • de+crepit(破裂声 )→破裂掉 →破旧的

例句 • The aim is to remove the heaviest-polluting, most decrepit vehicles from the roads. (IELTS3,T4,R1)目标是清除公路上对环境污染最严重和最破旧的车辆 。

dedicate [’dedɪkeɪt]

释义 • v. to give or devote (oneself, time, effort, etc.) to (a noble cause or purpose) 把(时间和精力)用在……上，把……献给

词根 • de+dic(宣称 )+ate→宣称贡献时间精力 →把 (时间和精力 )用在 ……上

派生 • dedicated2 adj. 献身的 ，一心一意的

dedication1 n. 奉献 ，献身

例句 • Recently, however, it has been experiencing something of a renaissance, with renewed demand for original Bakelite objects in the collectors’ marketplace, and museums, societies and dedicated individuals once again appreciating the style and originality of this innovative material. (IELTS5,T2,R1)然而最近胶木藏品一直在经历某种复兴 ：收藏市场上重新出现了对原胶木藏品的需求 ；博物馆 、社团和有兴趣的个人又开始欣赏这种创新材料的风格和独特性 。

defer [dɪ’fɜː]

释义 • v. to delay sth. until a later time; postpone sth. 推迟，延期

同义 • postpone

搭配 • defer to (尤因尊敬而 )听从 ，接受 (观点或决定 )

派生 • deference n. 尊重 ，遵从 ，恭敬

deferential adj. 恭敬的 ，敬重的

例句 • You can take up this opportunity if you are presently enrolled, or finishing this year, or you have deferred a year of study. (IELTS5,TA,R2)无论你是现在被录取 ，或者今年即将完成学业 ，还是已经延长了一年的学习 ，你都可以利用这个机会 。

degenerate [dɪ’dʒenəreɪt]

释义 • v. to pass into a worse physical, mental or moral state than one which is considered normal or desirable 恶化 adj. having lost the physical, mental or moral qualities that are considered normal or desirable 堕落的，颓废的 n. a degenerate person or animal 堕落的人

词根 • de(否 )+generate(产生 )→不产生了 →恶化 ，退化

派生 • degeneration n. 恶化

degenerative adj. 恶化的

例句 • Similarly, although at least some cetaceans have taste buds, the nerves serving these have degenerated or are rudimentary. (IELTS4,T1,R3) 同样地 ，虽然至少还有一些鲸目动物具有味蕾 ，但是它们的味觉神经要么已经退化 ，要么就非常原始 。

delegate [’delɪɡɪt]

释义 • n. a person chosen or elected by others to express their views (e.g. at a meeting or conference) 代表 v. to choose sb. to carry out (duties, a task, etc.) 委任，授权，委托， choose or send sb. as a representative 委派……为代表

例句 • We do have a few rooms available for delegates at the conference centre, if you’ d like. (IELTS6,T4,L1) 我们在会议中心为代表们准备了一些房间 ，如果您想使用 ，我们可做安排 。

delightful [dɪ’laɪtfəl]

释义 • adj. giving delight令人愉快的；漂亮的

词根 • delight(快乐 )+ful(充满的 )→充满快乐元素的 →令人愉快的

派生 • delight1 n. 快乐 ，愉快 ，高兴 ；让人愉快的事 v. 使高兴 ，使愉快

delighted3 adj. 高兴的 ，欢喜的

delightfully adv. 漂亮地

例句 • Starting in Weldown, you and your friends can choose a delightful 10, 20 or 30 kilometre route. (IELTS5,TB,R1) 从 Weldown开始 ，你和你的朋友可以选择令人愉快的 10公里 、20公里或 30公里线路 。

dementia [dɪ’menʃə]

释义 • n. madness with loss of powers of thinking due to brain disease or injury 痴呆症

词根 • de(取消 )+ment(想 ，心智 )+ia(表示疾病的名词后缀 )→没有心智的病 →痴呆症

例句 • Other diseases of old age—dementia , stroke, arteriosclerosis and emphysema—are also troubling fewer and fewer people. (IELTS6,T2,R2) 患其它老年疾病 ，如痴呆症 、中风 、动脉硬化 (症 )和肺气肿的人也越来越少 。

ment 想，思考，心智：

mental adj. 心理的，精神的，心智的

mention v. 提起，提及

comment v.andandandandn. 评论

demographer [dɪ’mɒɡrəfə]

释义 • n. an expert in studying changes in numbers of births, marriages, deaths, etc. 人口统计学家

词根 • demo(人民 )+grapher(绘画者 )→绘画人口的人 →人口统计学家

派生 • demography n. 人口统计学

demographic2 adj. 人口统计学的 ，人口的

例句 • “It really raises the question of what should be considered normal ageing,” says Kenneth Manton, a demographer from Duke University in North Carolina. (IELTS6,T2,R2) “这实际上提出了什么是正常衰老这个问题 。”北卡罗莱纳州杜克大学的人口统计学家肯尼斯 · 曼顿说 。

demolish [dɪ’mɒlɪʃ]

释义 • v. to pull or knock down (a building, etc.) 破坏，拆除

词根 • demo(人民 )+lish→人民创造一切也会破坏一切 →破坏

派生 • demolition2 n. 拆毁 ，毁坏

例句 • Australian sports teams win more than their fair share of titles, demolishing rivals with seeming ease. (IELTS6,T1,R1)澳大利亚体育代表队获得了多项荣誉 ，他们看起来很容易地就击败了很多对手 。

denomination [dɪˌnɒmə’neɪʃən]

释义 • n. a religious group or sect 教派 ；a class or unit of measurement or money (硬币或钞票的)面额

例句 • These teller machines accept any denomination of coins or notes up to 0. (IELTS4,TB,R2) 这台柜员机接受任何面额在 50美元以上的硬币和纸币 。

deploy [dɪ’plɒɪ]

释义 • v. to move into the correct position for battle 部署，动员，调动 ；to use (sth.) effectively 施展，利用

词根 • de(apart)+ploy(重叠 )→把重叠的东西分开 →重新部署

派生 • deployment n. 部署

例句 • Matthews found that it was best to be mixed-handed—this is because a hockey stick must be deployed in two directions—it would be a drawback to have hand or eye favouring one side. (IELTS7,T2,L4) 马修发现双手都灵活是最好的 ——这是因为冰球杆必须操控在两个方向上 ，手或眼只习惯一边是不利的 。

deregulate [ˌdiː’reɡjʊleɪt]

释义 • v. to remove the regulations from (sth.) 撤销对……的管制规定

词根 • 已知 regular意为规则的 ，推出其动词为 regulate，管制 。de(取消 )+regulate(管制 )→取消管制

派生 • deregulation1 n. 撤销管制 ，解除管制

例句 • This started changing, however, in the mid-l970s, when America began to deregulate its transportation industry. (IELTS6,T1,R2) 但这种情况在 20世纪 70年代中期开始改变 ，这个时候美国开始取消对交通行业的管制 。

deserve [dɪ’zɜːv]

释义 • v. to be sth. or have done sth. for which one should receive (a reward, special treatment, etc); to be entitled to; to merit 应得，值得

词根 • de(强调 )+serve(服务 )→应享受的服务 →值得

同义 • earn, merit

例句 • Giftedness and genius deserve proper scientific research into their true nature so that all talent may be retained for the human race. (IELTS8,T3,R2) 天赋和天才值得适当的科学研究 ，以发现它们真正的性质 ，以便所有的才能能够被人类保留下来 。

desolate [’desələt]

释义 • adj . (of a place) uninhabited and giving an impression of bleak and dismal emptiness 无人烟的；荒凉的；凄凉的

词根 • de(fully)+sol(孤独 )+ate→使孤独的

派生 • desolation n . 荒芜 ，荒凉 ，孤寂 ，凄凉

例句 • In November 1677, Halley observed a transit of the innermost planet, Mercury, from the desolate island of St Helena in the South Pacific. (IELTS9,T2,R2) 1677年的 11月 ，哈雷在南太平洋荒无人烟的圣海伦娜岛观察到了距离太阳最近的水星 “凌日”。

despise [dɪs’paɪz]

释义 • v. to feel contempt for sb./sth.; to consider sb./sth. as worthless 鄙视，藐视，看不起

词根 • de(向下 )+spise(看 )→向下看 →藐视 ，看不起

例句 • It then fell from favor again during the 1950s, and was despised and destroyed in vast quantities. (IELTS5,T2,R1) 20世纪 50年代它失宠了 ，受到了鄙视 ，然后被大量摧毁 。

detach [dɪ’tætʃ]

释义 • v. to unfasten sth. from sth.; to disconnect sth. 拆下，使分离

词根 • 已知 attach意为贴上 ，附上 ，推出 tach意为附 ，贴 。de(去除 )+tach(附 ，贴 )→拆下 ，使分离

派生 • detached adj. 不带感情的 ，公正的 ，冷淡的 ，超然的 ；独立的 ，分开的

detachable adj. 可拆卸的 ，可分开的

detachment n. 冷静 ，超然 ，客观

例句 • The only other problem anyone could find, was that there were pictures which were simply stuck on and so could easily become detached . (IELTS5,T1,L2)还有另一个也是唯一一个问题 ，任何人都能发现 ，那就是有些画是印上去的 ，很容易脱落 。

detergent [dɪˈtɜ:dʒənt]

释义 • n . a water-soluble cleansing agent which combines with impurities and dirt to make them more soluble, and differs from soap in not forming a scum with the salts in hard water洗涤剂

词根 • de-（away）+terg（擦）+-ent（adj .）→擦掉的→洗涤剂

例句 • It’ s got all the cleaning equipment, brushes and detergent and so on. (IELTS11,T1, L1) 所有的清洗设备、刷子和洗衣粉等都齐全。

devoid [dɪˈvɔɪd]

释义 • adj . entirely lacking or free from缺乏的，没有的

词根 • de-（away）+void（空）→拿走而变得空缺→缺少的

搭配 • devoid of

例句 • In the 1970s and ’ 80s, Lal was studying soils in Africa so devoid of organic matter that the ground had become extremely hard, like cement. (IELTS11,T4, L4) 在20世纪70、80年代，拉尔在非洲研究因缺乏有机物质而变得像水泥一样超级硬的土壤。

devour [dɪ’vaʊə]

释义 • v. to eat (sth.) hungrily or greedily 狼吞虎咽地吃，吞食；挥霍 ；to destroy (sth.) 吞没

词根 • de(down)+vour(吃 )→吃下去 →吞食

派生 • devouring adj. 吞食的 ，猛烈的

例句 • A natural predator indigenous to India, Neodumetia sangawani, was found useful in controlling the Rhodes grass-scale insect that was devouring forage grass in many parts of the US. (IELTS8,T4,R2) 印度土著的自然捕食者 Neodumetia sangawani可以用来控制 Rhodes草地上的害虫 。这些害虫正吞噬着美国许多地区的饲用牧草 。

dictate [dɪk’teɪt]

释义 • v. to control or command 影响，控制 ；to state or order sth. with the force of authority 指定，命令 ；to say or read aloud (words to be typed, written down or recorded on tape) 口授，口述

派生 • dictation n. 口授 ，口述 ；命令 ，支配

dictator n. 独裁者 ，专政者 ；专横的人 ，霸道的人

dictatorial adj. 霸道的 ，专横的 ；独裁的 ，专制的

dictatorship n. 独裁统治 ，独裁政府 ；独裁国家

例句 • This, in essence, is the problem of modern sociobiology—to discover the degree to which hard-wired genetic programming dictates , or at least strongly biases, the interaction of animals and humans with their environment, that is, their behavior. (IELTS5,T1,R2) 这实际上是一个现代社会生物学的问题 ——目的是发现天生的基因序列在多大程度上支配或者至少是强烈影响着动物和人与其生存环境的互动关系 ，也就是说动物和人的行为 。

differentiate [ˌdɪfə’renʃɪeɪt]

释义 • v. to see or show (two things) to be different; show sth. to be different (from sth. else) 区分，区别 ；to be a mark of difference between (people or things); distinguish 使不同，是……间的差别

词根 • different(不同 )+iate(v .)→使不同

派生 • differ v. 不同于 ，有别于

differentiation n. 区别 ，不同

搭配 • differentiate sth. from sth. 使某事有别于某事

例句 • Another factor that may boost the prospects for artificial intelligence in the near future is that investors are now looking for firms using clever technology, rather than just a clever business model, to differentiate themselves. (IELTS5,T3,R3)在不久的将来 ，另一个可以促进人工智能发展的因素是 ，投资者们不是寻找那些只有良好运营模式的公司 ，而是在寻找使用先进技术的公司来显示自己的与众不同 。

dilapidate [dɪ’læpɪdeɪt]

释义 • v. to cause or allow (a building, automobile, etc.) to fall into a state of disrepair, as by misuse or neglect (often used passively)（使）荒废，（使部分）毁坏

例句 • Firefighters’ unions that in the past complained of dilapidated equipment, old fire engines, and insufficient blueprints for fire safety are now praising the state’ s commitment, noting that funding for firefighting has increased, despite huge cuts in many other programs. (IELTS10,T4,R1)消防工会过去一直抱怨设备破损 、消防车老旧 ，以及消防安全方案欠缺 ，但是现在他们对政府的投入大加赞赏 。他们表示尽管政府在很多其他项目上都削减了资金 ，但对消防的资金投入却增加了 。

dilemma [dɪ’lemə]

释义 • n. a situation in which one has to choose between two undesirable things or courses of action (进退两难的)窘境，困境

词根 • di(between)+lemma(假设 )→模棱两可的假设 →困境 ，窘境

搭配 • in dilemma 进退两难 ，进退维谷

同义 • difficulty, plight, problem

例句 • Whatever the cause, the dilemma is always the same: what happens if these new, external sources of income dry up. (IELTS5,T4,R1) 不论什么原因 ，困境都是相同的 ：如果这些新的外部收入来源枯竭了 ，那会出现怎样的情况 。

diligent [’dɪlɪdʒənt]

释义 • adj. showing care and effort (in what one does); hard-working 勤勉的，勤奋的，用功的

词根 • di(apart)+lig(选择 )+ent→仔细选择的 →认真的

派生 • diligence n. 勤奋 ，用功

例句 • Diligent preparation is also necessary to effectively answer any interview question. (IELTS8,TB, R2) 人们也需要做积极的准备来有效地回答任何面试问题 。

dilute [daɪ’luːt]

释义 • v. to make (a liquid or colour) thinner or weaker (by adding water or another liquid) 稀释，冲淡 ；to make (sth.) weaker in force, effect, etc. 削弱，降低 adj. weakened by diluting 冲淡的；减弱的

词根 • di(分开 )+lute(洗 )→洗开 →稀释

例句 • It dilutes its product so that it’ s just a little below the concentration it should be. (IELTS4,T2,L4) 它稀释了产品 ，使产品仅仅比应该具有的浓度稍低一点 。

diplomatic [ˌdɪpləˈmætɪk]

释义 • adj . of or concerning diplomacy 外交上的

派生 • diplomacy n .外交

diplomat n . 外交家

例句 • Silk was also used as diplomatic gifts by the emperor. (IELTS11,T3, R1) 国王也用丝绸作为外交礼物。

discontinue [ˌdɪskən’tɪnjuː]

释义 • v. (cause sth. to) come to an end; stop (doing sth) 停止，中断；终止提供

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+continue→停止 ，中断

例句 • If any of the following occur, discontinue taking the medicine and contact your doctor: dizziness, vomiting, blurred vision. (IELTS3,TB,R1)如果发生头晕 、呕吐和视线模糊等现象 ，请停止用药 ，并与医生联系 。

discouraging [dɪs’kʌrɪdʒɪŋ]

释义 • adj. (cause sth. to) come to an end; stop (doing sth) 令人泄气的，令人沮丧的

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+courag(e)(勇气 )+ing→令人气馁的

派生 • discourage1 v. 使泄气 ，使失去信心 ，使沮丧 ；阻拦 ，劝阻

discouragement n. 令人沮丧的事

discouraged2 adj. 沮丧的 ，灰心丧气的

例句 • Quite often, governments try to kill off a minority language by banning its use in public or discouraging its use in schools, all to promote national unity. (IELTS4,T2,R1) 政府经常试图以禁止在公共场合说少数民族语言或不鼓励在学校说少数民族语言的方式消灭这些语言 ，一切为了促进民族统一 。

disdain [dɪs’deɪn]

释义 • n. the feeling that sb./sth. is not good enough to deserve one’ s respect; contempt 鄙视，蔑视，轻视 v. to treat (sth./sb.) with disdain; despise 鄙视，蔑视，轻视 ；to refuse (doing/to do sth) because of one’ s disdain 不屑做……

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+dain(价值 )→不承认价值 →轻视

派生 • disdainful adj. 鄙视的 ，轻视的 ，蔑视的

例句 • Baekeland’ s invention, although treated with disdain in its early years, went on to enjoy an unparalleled popularity which lasted throughout the first half of the twentieth century. (IELTS5,T2,R1) Baekeland的发明虽然在早期不受重视 ，但后来的受欢迎程度无人能及 ，这种状态一直持续了整个 20世纪的前半叶 。

disguise [dɪs’ɡaɪz]

释义 • n. disguised condition; disguising 假装，伪装 ；a thing worn or used for disguising 伪装物 v. to make sb./sth. look or sound different from normal; give sb./sth. a false appearance 假装，扮作 ；to hide or cover up (e.g. one’ s real feelings or intentions) 隐瞒，隐蔽，掩饰

词根 • dis(not)+guise(举止 )→掩盖举止 →伪装

搭配 • in disguise 伪装起来

disguise in/with 用 ……伪装

同义 • mask, guise, feign, camouflage, conceal, hide, cover

例句 • If you must make a note of it, disguise it as something else—a telephone number, say. (IELTS8,TB,R1) 如果你必须做笔记 ，把它隐藏为其他东西 ，比如电话号码 。

disgusting [dɪs’gʌstɪŋ]

释义 • adj. causing disgust 令人厌恶的，令人作呕的；非常坏的

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+gust(风味 ，口味 )+ing(……性的 )→没有风味的 →令人厌恶的

派生 • disgust1 n. 反感 ，厌恶 ；恶心 ；愤慨 v. 使生气 ，使愤慨 ；使作呕 ，使恶心

disgusted adj. 愤慨的 ；厌恶的 ；作呕的 ，恶心的

例句 • The fact that jokes tap into our general evaluative machinery explains why the line between funny and disgusting , or funny and frightening, can be so fine. (IELTS5,T2,R2) 玩笑进入总体评价系统这一事实解释了为什么有趣和恶心或有趣和吓人之间的差别会如此细微 。

disillusioned [ˌdɪsɪ’luːʒənd]

释义 • adj. disappointed in sb./sth. that one had admired or believed in 不再抱幻想的，失望的；醒悟的

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+illusion(幻想 )+ed→没有幻想的 →失望的 ；醒悟的

派生 • disillusion v. 使醒悟 ；使幻想破灭 n. 醒悟 ；幻灭

disillusionment n. 不抱幻想 ，失望

例句 • A better educated and less accepting public has become disillusioned with the experts in general, and increasingly sceptical about science and empirically based knowledge, they said. (IELTS4,T2,R2) 受过更好教育 、更为挑剔的公众已经对专家感到失望了 ，他们说 ，对科学及以经验为基础的知识 ，他们越来越怀疑 。

disjunction [dɪs’dʒʌŋkʃən]

释义 • n. the act of disjoining or the condition of being disjointed 分离，分裂

词根 • join→junction连接 ，dis(否定 ，相反 )+junction(连接 )→不连接 →分裂

派生 • disjunctive adj. 转折的 ，反意的

例句 • Yet opinion polls suggest that many people nurture the belief that environmental standards are declining and four factors seem to cause this disjunction between perception and reality. (IELTS5,T1,R3)但是民意调查显示许多人认为环境标准正在下降 。有 4个因素造成这种感觉与实际之间不一致 。

disorganised [dɪs’ɔːgənaɪzd]

释义 • adj. badly organized or planned 杂乱无章的，无计划的；做事无条理的

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+organise(组织 )+ed(adj .)→没组织的 →杂乱无章的

例句 • Similarly, it may help to discuss a topic with other people, especially if you feel that you have insufficient ideas, or too many disorganised ideas. (IELTS6,TB,R2)同样地 ，它可以帮你与其他人讨论一个话题 ，特别是当你觉得没有足够的想法或想法太多却没有条理的时候 。

disparate [’dɪspərɪt]

释义 • adj. so different in kind or degree that they cannot be compared 迥然不同的，不相干的

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+par(相等 )+ate→不相等的 →迥然不同的

派生 • disparity n. 差异 ，差别

例句 • The expression provided an attractive but informative name for a research programme that encompassed such previously disparate fields as operations research, cybernetics, logic and computer science. (IELTS5,T3,R3) 这个表达给研究项目提供了引人注目并传递信息的名字 。这个研究项目囊括了以前各自独立的领域如运筹学 、控制论 、逻辑学和计算机科学 。

dispiriting [dɪ’spɪrɪtɪŋ]

释义 • adj. making sb. lose their hope or enthusiasm 令人气馁的，令人垂头丧气的

词根 • di(not)+spirit(精神 )+ing(令人 ……的 )→令人没有精神的 →令人气馁的

派生 • dispirit v. 使失望 ，使气馁

dispirited adj. 气馁的

例句 • You wake up in the middle of the night in a strange hotel miles away from home, disoriented most probably from jet lag, when even the most expensive surroundings can seem empty and dispiriting . (IELTS7,T3,L4) 你午夜醒来 ，在离家很远的陌生旅馆里 ，很可能因为时差的关系而迷失方向 ，这时候即便最昂贵的环境可能看起来也很空洞和令人沮丧 。

disproportionately [ˌdɪsprə’pɔːʃənɪtlɪ]

释义 • adv. relatively too large or small, etc; out of proportion 不成比例地

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+proportion(比例 )+ate(adj .)+ly(adv .)→不成比例地

派生 • disproportion n. 不成比例 ，不相称

disproportionate adj. 不成比例的

例句 • Countries still trade disproportionately with their geographic neighbours. (IELTS6,T1,R2) 各国与其在地理位置上的邻国之间的贸易依然是不成比例的 。

disqualify [dɪs’kwɒləfaɪ]

释义 • v. to prevent sb. from doing sth., usu. because he has broken a rule or is not able enough 取消……资格

词根 • dis(否定 ，相反 )+qualify(使有资格 )→取消资格

搭配 • disqualify sb. from doing sth.使某人没有资格做某事

派生 • disqualification n. 无资格 ，取消资格

例句 • Will this disqualify me from getting a student loan? (IELTS3,TB,R2) 这会让我无法得到学生贷款吗 ？

dissolve [dɪ’zɒlv]

释义 • v. to make (a solid) become liquid 溶解 ；to disappear; to fade away 解散，结束

词根 • dis(分开 )+solve(解决 )→分开解决 →溶解 ；解散

派生 • dissolution n. 取缔 ，解散 ，瓦解 ；消失

例句 • Basically you dissolve lots of salt into the water and watch the crystal’ s form. (IELTS4,T4,L3) 基本上你在水中溶解大量盐 ，然后就可以看到晶体的形式 。

distaste [dɪs’teɪst]

释义 • n. dislike; aversion 不喜欢，厌恶

词根 • dis(不 )+taste(喜欢 )→厌恶

同义 • disfavor

例句 • Stanley Milgram of Yale University tested 40 subjects from all walks of life for their willingness to obey instructions given by a leader in a situation in which the subjects might feel a personal distaste for the actions they were called upon to perform. (IELTS5,T1,R2)耶鲁大学的 Stanley Milgram对来自各个生活阶层的 40名被试者进行了测试 ，以测试他们在被要求做自己讨厌的事情的情况下遵守领导指令的意愿度 。

distort [dɪs’tɔːt]

释义 • v. to pull or twist (sth.) out of its usual shape 扭曲，使变形

词根 • dis(分开 )+tort(卷缠 ，扭 )→扭曲

派生 • distortion2 n. 歪曲 ，曲解 ；扭曲 ，变形 ，失真

distorted adj. 歪曲的

例句 • As Peter Derks, a psychologist at William and Mary College in Virginia, says: I like to think of humour as the distorted mirror of the mind. (IELTS5,T2,R2)正如弗吉尼亚威廉与玛丽学院的心理学家 Peter Derks所说 ：“我想把幽默看成人类思维的变形镜”。

distressing [dɪ’stresɪŋ]

释义 • adj. afflicted with or suffering distress 使人痛苦的，令人苦恼的

例句 • This is particularly distressing because time seems to be a vital factor in the appreciation of all art forms. (IELTS10,T2,R3)这是特别令人苦恼的 ，因为时间似乎是欣赏艺术作品的一个很重要的因素 。

divert [daɪ’vɜːt]

释义 • v. to turn sb./sth. from one course to another 转移 ；to entertain or amuse (sb.) 使消遣

词根 • di(分开 )+vert(转移 )→转移

派生 • diversion n. 转移注意力的事物 ，消遣活动

diverting adj. 有趣的 ，娱乐的

例句 • Most of the Nile water is diverted into more than 10,000 kilometres of irrigation canals and only a small proportion reaches the sea directly through the rivers in the delta. (IELTS5,T3,R2) 大部分尼罗河水都被转移到了长 10，000公里的灌溉运河 ，只有一小部分直接通过三角洲的河流流入大海 。

dizziness [’dɪzɪnɪs]

释义 • n. feeling as if everything is spinning around; unable to balance; confused 眩晕，头晕目眩

词根 • dizz(y)(眩晕的 )+ness(n .)→头晕目眩

派生 • dizzy1 adj. 头晕目眩的

dizzying adj. 使人糊涂的

例句 • If any of the following occur, discontinue taking the medicine and contact your doctor: dizziness , vomiting, blurred vision. (IELTS3,TB,R1) 如果发生头晕 、呕吐 、视线模糊等情况 ，请停止服药并与医生联系 。

dot [dɒt]

释义 • n. a small round mark 点，句号 v. to mark (sth.) with a dot 在……加点；点缀 ；to place (things or people) here and there; to scatter 布满，分布

例句 • Looking up they discovered that the ceiling was dotted with the lights of thousands of glow-worms. (IELTS5,TB,R3) 他们向上看的时候发现天花板上布满了成千上万只萤火虫发出的亮光 。

downside [’daʊnsaɪd]

释义 • n. a disadvantageous aspect 不利面，消极面

词根 • down(低的 )+side→低的一面 →消极面

反义 • upside, advantage

例句 • On the downside , the data also reveals failures in public health that have caused surges in some illnesses. (IELTS6,T2,R2) 在消极面 ，数据还显示了公共卫生方面的失败 ，这已经引起了某些疾病患病率的猛增 。

downwind [ˌdaʊn’wɪnd]

释义 • adj. in the direction in which the wind blows 顺风的 adv. 顺风地

词根 • down(下 )+wind(风 )→下风向 →顺风的

例句 • If bees were responding only to the scent, how could they also “sniff down” food hundreds of metres away from the hive, food which was sometimes downwind ? (IELTS4,TB,R3) 如果蜜蜂只对香味有反应 ，那它们怎么也能从蜂巢飞行数百米寻找那些有时候是处于顺风方向的食物呢 ？

drab [dræb]

释义 • adj. of a dull light brown 淡褐色的，灰黄色的 ；dull; uninteresting 单调的

例句 • Electrical manufacturers seized on its insulating properties, and consumers every-where relished its dazzling array of shades, delighted that they were now, at last, no longer restricted to the wood tones and drab browns of the pre-plastic era. (IELTS5,T2,R1) 电器制造商看中的是它的绝缘特性 ，各地的消费者喜欢的是它各种炫目的色调 。他们很高兴现在终于不再局限于前塑料时代的原木色和土褐色了 。

drastic [’dræstɪk]

释义 • adj. having a strong or violent effect 激烈的，猛烈的

派生 • drastically3 adv. 猛烈地

例句 • Despite the intuition that something drastic needs to be done about such a costly problem, economic analyses clearly show it will be far more expensive to cut carbon dioxide emissions radically than to pay the costs of adaptation to the increased temperatures. (IELTS5,T1,R3) 尽管直觉是需要采取强势措施处理这个高代价的问题 ，但经济分析清楚地表明 ：大量削减二氧化碳的排放量的代价比适应气候变暖付出的代价要大得多 。

dual [’djʊ(ː)əl]

释义 • adj. having two parts or aspects; double 双的；二重的；二元的；二体的，二联的；孪生的；复式的；加倍的

词根 • du(双 )+al→双重的

同义 • double, two-fold

例句 • By 1967, dual -purpose ships, carrying loose cargo in the hold and containers on the deck, were giving way to all-container vessels that moved thousands of boxes at a time. (IELTS6,T1,R2) 到 1967年止 ，双功能船 ，也就是在底层舱装散货 ，在甲板上装集装箱的船 ，逐渐被能够一次性运输成千上万个箱子的全集装箱船所取代 。

dump [dʌmp]

释义 • v. to put (sth. unwanted) in a place and leave as rubbish 倾倒(垃圾)；倾销抛售 ；to leave or abandon (sb.) 丢弃，摆脱 n. a place where rubbish may be unloaded and left; rubbish-heap 垃圾堆

例句 • And other ancient civilisations certainly knew about kites; as early as 1250 BC, the Chinese were using them to deliver messages and dump flaming debris on their foes. (IELTS7,T4,R1) 其他文明古国肯定也了解风筝 。早在公元前 1250年 ，中国人就用它们来传递消息 ，向敌人投掷燃烧的碎片 。

dwindle [’dwɪndl]

释义 • v. to become gradually less or smaller 缩减，减少

同义 • decrease, diminish

例句 • The impetus behind the development of these early plastics was generated by a number of factors—immense technological progress in the domain of chemistry, coupled with wider cultural changes, and the pragmatic need to find acceptable substitutes for dwindling supplies of luxury materials such as tortoiseshell and ivory. (IELTS5,T2,R1) 推动早期塑料发展的因素有很多 ：化学领域内的巨大进步 ；文化的巨大变化 ；找到取代龟壳和象牙这类日益减少的奢侈材料的现实需要 。

eagerly [’iːgəlɪ]

释义 • adv. in an eager way 热切地，渴望地

派生 • eager1 adj. 热切的 ，渴望的

eagerness n. 热切 ，渴望

例句 • Von Frisch knew from experiments by an earlier researcher that if he put out a bowl of sweet sugar syrup, bees might at first take some time to find it but, once they had done so, within the hour, hundreds of other bees would be eagerly taking the syrup. (IELTS4,TB,R3) Von Frisch从之前一位研究者的试验中得知如果他把一碗甜糖浆放在外面 ，那么蜜蜂一开始可能会花些时间找到它 ，但一旦找到 ，一个小时之内其它数百个蜜蜂就会飞来大快朵颐 。

earnest [’ɜːnɪst]

释义 • adj. serious; determined; not light-hearted 认真的，郑重的；坚决的

搭配 • in earnest 严肃的 ，一本正经的 ；诚挚的

派生 • earnestness n. 认真 ，郑重 ；坚决

earnestly adv. 认真地 ，郑重地 ；坚决地

例句 • Animals at play often use unique signs—tail-wagging in dogs, for example—to indicate that activity superficially resembling adult behaviour is not really in earnest . (IELTS4,T2,R3) 玩耍中的动物常常使用独特的信号 ——如狗摇尾巴 ——表明表面上很像成人行为的动作实际上并没有那么正经 。

eccentricity [ˌeksen’trɪsɪtɪ]

释义 • n. the quality of being eccentric; the strangeness of behaviour, etc. 古怪，怪癖，异常

词根 • ec(out脱离 )+cent(e)r+icity→脱离中心 →古怪 ，怪癖

派生 • eccentric2 adj. 古怪的 ，异常的 n. 行为古怪的人

例句 • For all its faults and eccentricities his two-volume work is a masterpiece and a landmark, in his own words, setting the orthography, displaying the analogy, regulating the structures, and ascertaining the significations of English words. (IELTS5,T1,R1) 虽然有缺陷和怪异之处 ，他的两卷作品依然是杰作 ，具有划时代的意义 ，用他自己的话来说就是 ：界定了拼字法 ，展示了类比 ，调整了结构 ，确保了英语词汇的重要性 。

edging [’edʒɪŋ]

释义 • n. a thing that forms the border or edge of sth. 边缘；边饰，花边

派生 • edge11 n. 边线 ，边缘 ；优势 v. 缓慢小心地移动 ；形成 ……的边

例句 • You should ensure your cot has only rounded or smooth edging without any sharp edges. (IELTS5,T1,L2)必须确保你的小床只有圆滑而光滑的边 ，没有锐利的棱角 。

edible [’edɪbəl]

释义 • adj. fit to be eaten可以吃的，适合吃的

词根 • ed(吃 )+ible(可 ……的 )→可吃的

派生 • edibility n. 可食用性

例句 • The ants cultivate a large number of different species of edible fungi. (IELTS7,T3,R1) 那些蚂蚁培育了大量不同种类的食用菌 。

ejection [ɪ’dʒekʃən]

释义 • n. to make someone leave a place or building by using force 驱逐，赶出 ；the act of ejecting or the condition of being ejected 弹出，喷射，喷出物

词根 • e(出来 )+ject(扔 ，投 )+ion(n .)→被扔出来 →逐出

派生 • eject v. 射出 ，弹出 ；驱逐

例句 • The reaction to the ejection of these small particles causes the rocket to move forwards. (IELTS3,T1,R1) 这些小粒子喷发的反作用力使火箭向前运动 。

elapse [ɪ’læps]

释义 • v. if a period of time elapses, it passes (时间)过去，流逝

词根 • e(出来 )+lapse(溜走 )→时光溜走 →逝去

例句 • The time that elapses before failure occurs is unpredictable. (IELTS5,T4,R2) 失败之前流逝的时间不可预测 。

elastic [ɪ’læstɪk]

释义 • adj. returning to its normal or previous size or shape after being pulled or pressed 有弹性的，有弹力的 ；not fixed or unalterable; adaptable; flexible 灵活的，可伸缩的 n. elastic cord or material, usu. made with rubber thread 橡皮带，松紧带

词根 • e(出来 )+last(延长 )+ic→能够延长的 →有弹力的

派生 • elasticity n. 弹力 ，弹性 ；灵活性 ，适应性

例句 • Sharks have a different structure to most fish: instead of a skeleton made of bone, they have a tough elastic skeleton of cartilage. (IELTS4,T4,L4)鲨鱼的骨髓结构与大多数鱼都不一样 ：它的骨架不是由骨头构成 ，而由强韧且富有弹性的软骨组成 。

elicit [ɪ’lɪsɪt]

释义 • v. to draw (facts, a response, etc.) from sb., sometimes with difficulty 诱出，探出(事实、反应等)

词根 • e(出来 )+licit(引导 )→引出 →诱出

派生 • elicitation1 n. 诱导 ，诱出

例句 • Often, the researcher wishes to obtain information about just a single variable, in which case a restricted set of questions may be used: a particular feature of pronunciation, for example, can be elicited by asking the informant to say a restricted set of words. (IELTS4,T3,R3)通常研究者希望获得关于某个单音的信息 ，在这种情况下可以使用一套严格的问题 ：如通过让被调查者朗读一套限定的词汇的方法来得出其发音的特点 。

eligibility [’elɪdʒəbɪlɪtɪ]

释义 • n. the state of being eligible 合格，适宜；资格

词根 • e(出来 )+lig(=lect选择 )+ibility→能够被选择出来的 →合格 ，适宜

派生 • eligible10 adj. 符合条件的 ，合适的

例句 • Although the loan is intended to supplement the grant for living costs, eligibility for a student loan is not restricted to those who receive a maintenance grant. (IELTS3,TB,R2)虽然贷款的目的是为了补贴生活开支 ，但是学生贷款的资格不仅限于那些接受生活补助金的学生 。

elitist [eɪ’liːtɪst]

释义 • adj. of the elite or elitism 精英主义的 n. a person who believes in elitism 精英主义者

词根 • e(出来 )+lit(挑选 )+ist(主义者 )→挑选出人才的主义 →精英主义

派生 • elite n. 精英 ，上层人士 adj. 精英的 ，精锐的

elitism n. 精英统治论 ，精英主义

例句 • A largish minority were strongly against it, claiming that it is elitist and a waste of funds. (IELTS4,T3,L4) 很大一部分少数派强烈反对 ，声称这是精英主义 ，是对资金的浪费 。

eloquently [’eləkwəntlɪ]

释义 • adv . in a fluent or persuasive manner善辩地，富于表现力地

词根 • e-（out）+loqu（说）+ent（adj. ）+ly（adv. ）→滔滔不绝地说→雄辩地

例句 • No one since has celebrated more eloquently the magnitude of its achievement. (IELTS11,T4, R3) 此后再无人能够如此精妙地形容这项成就的伟大。

elucidate [ɪ’luːsɪdeɪt]

词根 • e(出来 )+lucid(清晰 )+ate→弄清楚 →阐明 ，说明

派生 • elucidation n. 阐明 ，说明

例句 • Put another way, sociobiology is concerned with elucidating the biological basis of all behavior. (IELTS5,T1,R2) 换言之 ，社会生物学致力于阐明所有行为的生物学基础 。

embarrassment [ɪm’bærəsmənt]

释义 • n. embarrassing or being embarrassed 尴尬，难堪，窘迫 ；a person or thing that embarrasses 使人为难的事

词根 • em(in)+barr(栏 )+ass(v.)+ment→被拦住 →难堪 ，窘迫

派生 • embarrass v. 使窘迫 ，使困扰 ；妨碍 ，牵累

embarrassed1 adj. 困惑的 ，难堪的

embarrassing1 adj. 令人难堪的

例句 • Ants are so much like human beings as to be an embarrassment . (IELTS7,T3,R1) 蚂蚁的确太像人了 ，这真让人尴尬 。

embassy [’embəsɪ]

释义 • n. an ambassador and his staff 大使馆，使馆工作人员

例句 • Why don’ t we call the embassy ? (IELTS7,T4,L3) 为什么我们不打电话给使馆工作人员 ？

embellish [ɪm’belɪʃ]

释义 • v. to beautify by or as if by ornamentation; ornament; adorn 修饰；润色；装饰

例句 • But perhaps the most impressive features are the intricate decorative sculptures that embellish many stepwells, showing activities from fighting and dancing to everyday acts such as women combing their hair or churning butter. (IELTS10,T1,R1)但最令人印象深刻的特征可能是那些精致的装饰性雕塑 ，这些雕塑展示了人们的各种活动 ，从战斗和跳舞到日常活动 ，如妇女梳头或搅拌黄油 。

embezzlement [ɪm’bezəlmənt]

释义 • n. embezzling 盗用，挪用(公款)，侵吞

词根 • em(出来 )+bezzle(破坏 )+ment→实施破坏 →盗用 ，侵吞

派生 • embezzle v. 盗用 ，挪用 (公款 )，侵吞

例句 • So crimes like theft by employees—things like embezzlement or fraud against one’ s actual employer are excluded according to this definition. (IELTS4,T2,L4) 所以根据这一定义 ，员工的盗窃行为 ——如挪用公款或欺诈实际雇主等行为被排除在外 。

emblazoned [ɪm’bleɪzənd]

释义 • adj. if something is emblazoned with a name, design etc, it has that design on it where it can easily be seen (印刷、绘制、装饰得)十分显眼的，醒目的

例句 • Rarely do patients watch a doctor write with a pen that isn’ t emblazoned with a drug’ s name. (IELTS6,T4,R1) 病人很少看到医生会用一支没有标记某种药品的名称的笔写字 。

embryonic [ˌembriˈɒnɪk]

派生 • embryo n . 胚胎

例句 • Other epigenetic processes appear to occur randomly, while others are normal, such as those that guide embryonic cells as they become heart, brain, or liver cells, for example. (IELTS11,T4,R1) 其他一些后成遗传过程似乎发生得比较随机，还有另外一些是很正常的，比如有些后成遗传过程能够引导胚胎细胞形成心脏、大脑或肝脏细胞之类的。

emergent [ɪ’mɜːdʒənt]

释义 • adj. emerging 刚出现的，新兴的

词根 • e(出来 )+merge(浸没 )+ent(adj .)→从浸没中出来的 →刚出现的 ，新兴的

派生 • emerge17 v. 出现 ，显露 ，暴露

emerging4 adj. 新兴的

例句 • The emergent nation states of Europe developed competitive interests in world exploration and the development of trade. (IELTS5,T2,R3) 欧洲新兴国家对探索世界和贸易发展竞相产生了兴趣 。

emeritus [ɪ(ː)’merɪtəs]

释义 • adj. retired, but keeping his title as an honour 荣誉退休的

例句 • Identifying genetically talented individuals is only the first step, Michael Yessis, an emeritus professor of Sports Science at California State University at Fullerton, maintains that genetics only determines about one third of what an athlete can do. (IELTS4,T4,R1) 从基因上确定天才运动员只是第一步 ， 位于富尔敦加州州立大学运动科学系的荣誉教授 Michael Yessis 认为 ， 一个运动员所取得的成就中只有三分之一是由基因决定的 。

eminent [’emɪnənt]

同义 • famous, distinguished

派生 • eminence n . 卓越 ，杰出

例句 • His talent and devotion to the subject were perceived by his teacher, Thomas Hall, who encouraged him to attend a series of lectures given by the eminent scientist Michael Faraday at the Royal Institution. (IELTS9,T1,R1) 珀金的老师托马斯 · 霍尔发觉了他在化学方面的天赋以及对这一学科的热衷 ，于是就鼓励他去听著名科学家迈克尔 · 法拉第在英国皇家研究所的一系列讲座 。

empirical [ɪm’pɪrɪkəl]

empirically1 adv. 经验主义地

例句 • Some of these scholars, including two with interests in language—John Wallis and John Wilkins—helped found the Royal Society in 1660 in order to promote empirical scientific research. (IELTS5,T2,R3) 一些学者 ，包括两个对语言感兴趣的学者 ——John Wallis和 John Wilkins——于 1660帮助建立了皇家学会 ，以推动经验科学研究的发展 。

encapsulate [ɪn’kæpsjəleɪt]

释义 • v. to express sth. briefly; to summarize sth. 压缩，概括

词根 • 已知 capsule为胶囊 ，en(v .进入 )+capsul(e)+ate→压缩为胶囊 →压缩 ，概括

派生 • encapsulation n. 压缩 ，概括

例句 • HAL thus encapsulated the optimism of the 1960s that intelligent computers would be widespread by 2001. (IELTS5,T3,R3)因此 HAL是对 20世纪 60年代认为智能电脑将在 2001年广泛使用这种乐观主义的概括 。

endeavour [ɪn’devə]

词根 • en(强调作用 )+deavour(职责 )→使尽责 →尽力

例句 • In addition, the managers, assistant managers, supervisors and assistant supervisors of these two divisions were trained in group methods of leadership, which they endeavoured to use as much as their skill would permit during the experimental year. (IELTS3,T4,R3) 另外 ， 两个部门的经理 、 经理助理 、 督导 、 督导助理集体接受了领导艺术的培训 。 在接下来的试验年中 ， 他们要在自己能力允许的范围内努力运用自己所学到的技能 。

endorse [en’dɔ:s]

词根 • en(in)+ dorse (背面 )→写在背面

派生 • endorsement n . 赞同 ，支持 ，签名

例句 • We estimated that it was about one fifth, and this was endorsed by looking at large-scale usage maps in the town land survey office—24% to be precise. (IELTS9,T4,L4) 我们估计差不多是五分之一 。这与城镇土地调查办公室大规模使用的地图相互映证 ——准确地说是 24%。

enervation [ˌenə’veɪʃən]

释义 • n. weakening and loss of energy削弱，衰弱

例句 • The cost is in the collateral damage of the very methods of food production that have made the food cheaper: in the pollution of water, the enervation of soil, the destruction of wildlife, the harm to animal welfare and the threat to human health caused by modern industrial agriculture. (IELTS7,T2,R2) 所付出的代价是降低食品价格的食品生产方式附带的损害 ：现代农业工业化引起的水污染 、土壤弱化 、野生动植物破坏 、损坏动物健康 、威胁人类健康 。

enforcement [ɪn’fɔːsmənt]

派生 • enforce3 v. 实施 ，执行 ；强制 ，迫使

enfranchise [ɪn’fræntʃaɪz]

engross [ɪn’grəʊs]

释义 • v. to occupy all the time or attention of (sb.) 使全神贯注，使埋头于

词根 • en(in)+gross(全部 )→全身心地投入其中

派生 • engrossed adj. 全神贯注的 ，专心致志的

enigma [ɪ’nɪgmə]

enlighten [ɪn’laɪtn]

释义 • v. to give more knowledge or information to sb.; to free sb. from false beliefs or ignorance 启发，开导

词根 • en(使 ……)+light(灯光 ，光明 )+en(v .)→使点亮 ，照亮 →启发 ，开导

派生 • enlightenment n. 启发 ，开导

例句 • In less enlightened countries, and in the European Union, the trend has been to reduce rather than eliminate subsidies. (IELTS3,T2,R2) 在开化程度较低的国家以及欧盟 ，趋势是降低而不是消除补助金 。

ensue [ɪn’sjuː]

释义 • v. to happen afterwards or as a result; follow 接着发生，接踵而至

词根 • en(in)+sue(跟随 )→跟着进来 →接踵而至

entice [ɪn’taɪs]

释义 • v. to try to tempt or persuade sb., usu. by offering sth. pleasant or a reward 引诱；怂恿，教唆

同义 • induce, lure, tempt

派生 • enticement n. 诱使 ，诱惑

例句 • Management is able to use the growth to entice and encourage employees. (IELTS6,T3,R2) 管理层能够使用增长的数据去引导和鼓励员工 。

entrust [ɪn’trʌst]

释义 • v. to trust sb. to take charge of sth./sb. 委托；信任

词根 • en(in)+trust(相信 )→相信 →信任

例句 • As a hotelier, how do you go about attracting people to give up the security of their own home and entrust themselves to staying in a completely strange place and sleeping in an unfamiliar bed? (IELTS7,T3,L4) 作为旅馆从业者 ，你怎样吸引人们 ，使他们放弃自己家的安全感而安心呆在完全陌生的旅馆里 ，睡在不熟悉的床上呢 ？

entwine [ɪn’twaɪn]

释义 • v. to wind one thing with or round another 盘绕，使盘绕，使交错

词根 • en(in)+twine(缠绕 )→盘绕

例句 • The history of human civilisation is entwined with the history of the ways we have learned to manipulate water resources. (IELTS7,T1,R2) 人类文明的历史是和我们学会如何处理水资源的历史交织在一起的 。

envisage [ɪn’vɪzɪdʒ]

释义 • v. to picture (an event, action, etc.) in the mind as a future possibility; imagine 展望，想象；面对

词根 • en(使 ……)+vis(看 )+age(行为 )→展望 ，想象

同义 • envision

例句 • It’ s just a chance for you to say anything about the equipment, and problems you envisage . (IELTS3,T3,L3) 这只是一个陈述你对设备的看法以及你预见到的问题的机会 。

epitomise [ɪ’pɪtəmaɪz]

释义 • v. to be an epitome of (sth.) 集中体现，概括

词根 • epi(on)+tome(cut，剪切 )+ise→剪切后剩下的精华部分 →概括

派生 • epitome n. 缩影 ，梗概 ，摘要

例句 • Indeed, in many respects the Siriono epitomise the popular conception of life in Amazonia. (IELTS3,T3,R2)事实上 ，从很多方面来看 ，西里奥诺人的生活集中体现了亚马逊河流域普遍的生活理念 。

equality [ɪ’kwɒlɪtɪ]

释义 • n. the state of being equal 同等，平等

派生 • equal5 adj. 同等的 ；平等的

equally9 adv. 同等地 ，平等地

equation2 n. 等式 ，方程式 ；平衡

equator2 n. 赤道

例句 • It also conveys a sense of the energy and ability the suffragettes brought to their fight for freedom and equality . (IELTS3,T4,R2) 它也传递了妇女参政权论者在争取自由和平等时的精神和能力 。

equilibrium [ˌiːkwə’lɪbrɪəm]

释义 • n. the state of being balanced 平衡，均势

词根 • equi(平等 )+libr(平衡 )+ium→平衡

例句 • An organism is an open, dynamic system through which new material continuously flows, destruction of old material and formation of new material are thus in permanent dynamic equilibrium . (IELTS8,T3,R3) 有机体是一个开放 、动态的系统 。通过这个系统 ，新的物质不断地流动 ，旧事物的毁灭和新事物的产生因此处在动态的平衡中 。

erupt [ɪ’rʌpt]

释义 • v. to suddenly throw out lava, etc. (火山等)爆发，迸发，喷出；突然发生

词根 • e(out)+rupt(break断裂 )→爆发

派生 • eruption14 n. 爆发 ，迸发 ，喷发

例句 • When Mount Pinatubo suddenly erupted on 9 June 1991, the power of volcanoes past and present again hit the headlines. (IELTS4,T3,R2) 当 Pinatubo火山于 1991年 6月 9日突然爆发的时候 ，关于过去和现在火山威力的报道又成了头条 。

ethereal [ɪ’θɪərɪəl]

释义 • adj. of unearthly delicacy and lightness; seeming too spiritual or fairy-like for this world 飘渺的；超凡的

例句 • “We can’ t waste our time looking at ethereal scientific questions that don’ t help the coach work with an athlete and improve performance,” says Peter Fricker, chief of science at AIS. (IELTS6,T1,R1) “我们不能浪费时间关注那些不能提高运动员训练水平和改进运动员表现的缥缈的问题 ，”Peter Fricker，AIS的科学主管如此说到 。

ethnicity [eθ’nɪsɪtɪ]

释义 • n. ethnic character, background, or affiliation 种族，民族

派生 • ethnic1 adj. 种族的 ，民族的

例句 • It should be noted that the two groups of children had been carefully matched by the investigators so that they were comparable in age, ethnicity , race, and social class. (IELTS7,T4,R3) 应该注意的是 ，调查者已经对两组儿童进行了认真的分配 ，使他们在年纪 、民族 、种族和社会阶层方面具有可比较性 。

evil [’iːvəl]

释义 • adj. morally bad; wicked 凶恶的，邪恶的 ；very unpleasant or harmful 道德败坏的，危害社会的；令人厌恶的 n. a wrongdoing or wickedness 邪恶，恶行

同义 • bad, sinful, ill, wicked, vicious, harmful

例句 • An action such as shocking a victim, which in isolation appears evil, acquires a completely different meaning when placed in this setting. (IELTS5,T1,R2) 孤立地看 ，恐吓受害者是邪恶的行为 ，在这种情况下会 ，它会有完全不同的含义 。

excavate [’ekskəveɪt]

释义 • v. wrongdoing or wickedness 挖洞，开凿，挖掘，使……出土

词根 • ex(out)+cav(洞 )+ate→挖出洞

派生 • excavation5 n. 挖洞 ，开凿 ，挖掘

例句 • Some large species originating from France excavate tunnels to a depth of approximately 30cm below the dung pat. (IELTS3,T2,R1) 一些源于法国的大的物种能将隧道挖掘到屎堆以下约 30厘米的深度 。

expiry [ɪk’spaɪərɪ]

释义 • n. an ending, esp. of the period when a contract or agreement is in force 终止，期满

词根 • ex(out)+pire(呼吸 )+y→吐出气体 →呼出最后一口气 →终止 ，期满

派生 • expire2 v. 期满 ，失效 ；死亡 ，断气

例句 • Expiry date: 16 February, 2004. (IELTS3,TB,R1) 截止日期 ：2004年 2月 16日 。

extracurricular [ˌekstrəkə’rɪkjʊlə]

词根 • extra(额外的 )+curricular(课程的 )→课外的

例句 • What role do you think extracurricular activities play in education? (IELTS3,T1,S3) 你认为课外活动在教育中起什么作用 ？

extrapolation [ɪksˌtræpə’leɪʃən]

释义 • n. calculating (an unknown quantity) approximately from known values or measurements 推测，推断，推知

词根 • extra(外面 )+pol(放 )+ation→预先放在外面 →推测

派生 • extrapolate v. 推测 ，推断 ，推知

例句 • As a consequence, during the 1980s a kind of doomsday scenario (analogous to similar doomsday extrapolations about energy needs and fossil fuels or about population increases) was projected by health administrators, economists and politicians. (IELTS4,T4,R3) 因此 ，在 20世纪 80年代期间 ，健康管理者 、经济学家和政治家设想了一种世界末日的情况 (与关于能源需要 、矿物燃料或关于人口增长的末日推测类似 )。

extravagance [ɪk’strævəgəns]

释义 • n. being extravagant 奢侈，铺张，浪费 ；an extravagant thing, act, statement, etc. 奢侈品，过度，放肆

词根 • extra(超过 )+vag(游荡 )+ance→游荡到外面 →过度 ，过分 ，放肆

派生 • extravagant adj. 奢侈的 ，浪费的

extravagantly adv. 浪费地 ；放肆地

例句 • Are doctors to blame for the escalating extravagance of pharmaceutical marketing? (IELTS6,T4,R1) 对于医药市场不断升级的挥霍情况 ，医生应该受到谴责吗 ？

extrusion [ɪk’struːʒən]

释义 • n. the act of forcing or squeezing out sth. under pressure 挤出

词根 • ex(向外 )+trusion(推出 )→向外推 →挤出

派生 • extrude v. 挤出

反义 • intrusion

例句 • Sometimes it is slow: vast bubbles of magma—molten rock from the mantle-inch towards the surface, cooling slowly, to show through as granite extrusions . (IELTS4,T3,R2) 有时候过程很慢 ，巨大的岩浆泡 ——熔融岩石从地幔溢到表面 ，慢慢冷却 ，以花岗岩喷出物的形式显现出来 。

rude/trus 插入，推：

intrude v. 侵略

intrusion n. 侵入

protrude1 v. 突出，伸出

protrusive adj. 伸出的，突

出的

exuberant [ɪg’zjuːbərənt]

词根 • ex(out)+uber(富有成果的 )+ant→有成就的 →高兴的

派生 • exuberance n. 生气勃勃 ，充满生机

exuberantly adv. 充满生气地 ，生气勃勃地

例句 • Play may look like a carefree and exuberant way to pass the time before the hard work of adulthood comes along, but there’ s much more to it than that. (IELTS4,T2,R3) 在成年阶段辛苦劳作来临之前 ，游戏可能看起来像是以无忧无虑 、充满活力的方式去度过时间 ，但游戏的意义远大于此 。

词根 • famil(家人 )+iarise(使 ……化 )→使家人化 →使熟悉 ，使通晓

搭配 • familiarise yourself with sth. 让你自己熟悉某物

派生 • familiar46 adj. 熟悉的

feminism [’femɪnɪzəm]

fickle [’fɪkəl]

fidelity [fɪ’deləti]

释义 • n. the degree of accuracy with which sound or images are recorded or reproduced 忠实；逼真； 保真度

例句 • If appropriate works of fine art could be rendered permanently accessible to the public by means of high-fidelity reproductions, as literature and music already are, the public may feel somewhat less in awe of them. (IELTS10,T2,R3)如果能像文学和音乐那样 ，通过高质量的仿品把艺术品永久性地普及给大众 ，也许人们能对艺术品少些畏怯 。

filler [’fɪlə]

词根 • fill(填充 )+er→填充物

派生 • fill2 v. 填充 ，填满 ，塞满

finitude [’faɪnɪtjuːd]

flavour [’fleɪvə]

释义 • n. a taste and smell, esp. of food 味道，风味； a special quality, characteristic or atmosphere 特色 v. to give flavour to sth. by adding herbs, spices, etc. 给……调味

fledging [fledʒɪŋ]

释义 • n. a young bird that is just able to fly 羽毛初长的雏鸟，刚会飞的幼鸟 ；an inexperienced person 无经验的人

flimsy [’flɪmzɪ]

释义 • adj. light and thin轻而薄的 ；not strong or solid enough for the purpose for which it is used 脆弱的，易损坏的

flip [flɪp]

释义 • v. to throw or toss with a light, brisk motion 掷，弹，轻击 ；to turn a somersault in the air 空翻 n. the act of flipping, especially 抛，弹 ；a somersault 筋斗

搭配 • flip through 草草翻阅 ，浏览

flip side 事物不太重要的方面

(IELTS7,TA,R3) Florence可以帮助神经学家理解他们所谓的注意力处理 ，也就是决定一个人所注意的东西以及注意时长的大脑机制 ，以及不太重要的方面 ，如注意力缺乏症和多动症的问题 。

flock [flɒk]

fluent [’fluːənt]

词根 • flu(流 )+ent(adj. )→流动的 →流利的

派生 • fluency2 n. 流利度 ，流畅

flustered [’flʌstəd]

派生 • fluster v. 使人不知所措 ，使难堪 ，使紧张

例句 • How can we possibly account for this vast discrepancy between what calm, rational, knowledgeable people predict in the comfort of their study and what pressured, flustered , but cooperative teachers actually do in the laboratory of real life? (IELTS5,T1,R2) 一方面是平静 、理性 、知识丰富的人在舒服的书房里做出的预测 ，一方面有压力的 、不知所措但可以合作的老师在真实的实验室里的情况 。我们怎么能够解释他们之间的巨大差异呢 ？

foe [fəʊ]

foil [fɒɪl]

footage [’fʊtɪdʒ]

释义 • n. length of film made for the cinema or TV (某一主题或事件的)影片 ；length or distance measured in feet (尤指店铺等以平方英尺表示的)面积

词根 • foot+age(表示集合名词或总称 )→用脚丈量 →尺数 ，长度

例句 • Original newsreel footage shows the suffragette Emily Wilding Davison throwing herself under King George V’ s horse at a famous racecourse. (IELTS3,T4,R2) 原始的新闻片显示 ，女性参政论者 Emily Wilding Davison在一个著名的赛马场突然扑倒在乔治五世的马下 。

-age 表示集合名词或总称：

wordage n. 文字，词汇量

percentage n. 百分比

onnage n. 吨数，吨位

mileage n. 英里数

acreage n. 英亩数

assemblage n. 集合的人群

leafage n. 叶子

foregone conclusion [fɔː’ɡɒn kən’kluːʒən]

释义 • phr. result that can be predicted with certainty 必然结局；不出意料的结果

例句 • I think it can but it’ s not a foregone conclusion unless they manage to attract the right level of investment. (IELTS5,T4,L3) 我认为这有可能但并不是一个必然的结论 ，除非他们努力吸引恰当程度的投资 。

forfeit [’fɔːfɪt]

释义 • v. to subject to seizure as a forfeit 被罚，没收 n. something (to be) paid or given up as a penalty or punishment 罚款

词根 • for(out)+feit(做 )

派生 • forfeiture n. 没收 ，丧失

例句 • Students forfeit tuition if they arrive late, are absent or leave before the course ends. (IELTS3,TA,R2) 学生如果迟到 、缺课或者早退的话就会被罚学费 。

forgive [fə’ɡɪv]

释义 • v. to stop being angry or bitter towards sb. or about sth.; to stop blaming or wanting to punish sb. 原谅，饶恕，宽恕 ；to say that sb. need not repay (the money owed); not demand repayment from (sb.) 免除(债务等)

词根 • for(away)+give→give away(就此作罢 )→原谅

搭配 • forgive sb. for doing sth.原谅某人做某事

派生 • forgivable adj. 可宽恕的 ，可原谅的

forgiveness n. 原谅 ，饶恕 ，宽恕

例句 • And you would be forgiven for thinking this, because in fact most lions do come from Africa. (IELTS6,T4,L4) 你这么想也可以理解 ，因为实际上大多数狮子确实都来自非洲 。

forgo [fɔː’gəʊ]

释义 • v. to give up or do without 放弃，抛弃

词根 • for(away)+go→go away→走开 →放弃 ，抛弃

例句 • Here we have two radically different explanations for why so many teacher-subjects were willing to forgo their sense of personal responsibility for the sake of an institutional authority figure. (IELTS5,T1,R2) 对于为什么这么多作为研究对象的教师愿意因为学院权威放弃自己的个人责任感 ，我们有两种完全不同的解释 。

formality [fɔː’mælɪtɪ]

释义 • n. careful observance of rules, conventions, etc. of language or behaviour 拘泥形式，礼节，礼仪 ； the action required by convention or law 正规(形式上的)手续

词根 • form(形式 )+ality→形式上 →拘泥形式

派生 • form141 n. 形式 v. 形成

formal10 adj. 正式的

formally1 adv. 正式地

format3 n. 板式 ，编排 v. 设计

formation5 n. 形成 ；队形 ；组织 ；形成物

formative1 adj. 形成性的

例句 • In social circumstances, dress has often been used as a role sign to indicate the nature and degree of formality of any gathering and occasionally the social status of people present. (IELTS3,T2,R3) 在社会环境中 ，衣着一直象征聚会的性质和正式程度 ，有时候象征着出席者的社会地位 。

派生 • formulate5 v. 系统地阐述 ，明确地表达

formula2 n. 公式

例句 • The myth of scientific method is that it is inductive: that the formulation of scientific theory starts with the basic, raw evidence of the senses—simple, unbiased, unprejudiced observation. (IELTS3,T1,R3) 科学方法的神奇之处在于它是归纳式的 ：科学理论的系统阐述开始于基本的 、原始的感官证据 ——简单 、客观 、公正的观察 。

forthcoming [ˌfɔːθ’kʌmɪŋ]

释义 • adj. about to happen or appear in the near future 即将到来的

词根 • forth(往前 )+coming→即将到来的

例句 • Photographs depict vivid scenes of a suffragette’ s life: WSPU members on a self-proclaimed monster march, wearing their official uniforms of a white frock decorated with purple, white and green accessories; women selling The Suffragette at street corners, or chalking up pavements with details of a forthcoming meeting. (IELTS3,T4,R2) 照片生动地描述了女性参政论者生活的景象 ：妇女社会政治联盟成员走在自发形成的庞大队伍中 ，穿着她们正式的白色连衣裙制服 ，上面有紫色 、白色和绿色的配饰 ；妇女在街角销售 《妇女解放报 》，或者在路面上用粉笔写下下次会议的详细信息 。

fortnight [’fɔːtnaɪt]

释义 • n. two weeks 两周，十四天

联想 • fort(看做 fourteen)+night→十四个日夜

例句 • I seem to remember when we did it at high school we had to wait up to a fortnight before we saw any halfway decent results. (IELTS4,T4,L3) 我似乎记得我们上中学的时候 ，必须等待 2周才能看到并不怎么体面的结果 。

fossilise [’fɒsəlaɪz]

释义 • v. to become a fossil使成化石，变成化石；（使）僵化

词根 • fossil(化石 )+ise(……化 )→使成化石

派生 • fossil18 n. 化石

fossilisation1 n. 成化石 ，化石化

例句 • Fireflies very similar to those we see today have been found fossilised in rocks which were formed about 30 million years ago, and their ancestors were probably glowing long before then. (IELTS5,TB,R3) 萤火虫与那些我们今天在化石里看到的 、形成于 3000万年前的东西非常相似 。他们的祖先可能在那之前很久就开始发光了 。

fourfold [’fɔːfəʊld]

词根 • four+fold(折 ，翻 )→四倍

例句 • In the USA, industrial production has risen fourfold since 1950, while water consumption has fallen by more than a third. (IELTS6,TA,R3) 在美国 ，工业生产总值自 1950年以来已经上升到 4倍 ，而水的消耗量下降了超过 1/3。

fraction [’frækʃən]

释义 • n. a small part, bit, amount, or proportion (of sth) 小部分，片断，碎片 ；very small; trivial or unimportant 一点儿，一些 ；a precise division of a number 分数

词根 • fract(打破 )+ion→打破的东西 →碎片

同义 • portion, paticle

派生 • fractional adj. 部分的 ；分数的 ；轻微的 ，无足轻重的

例句 • However, using light to find one’ s own way around requires vastly more energy, since the eyes have to detect the tiny fraction of the light that bounces off each part of the scene. (IELTS7,T1,R1) 但是 ，在灯光帮助下找路需要更多精力 ，因为眼睛必须分辨由景象的每一部分反射的微弱亮光 。

fragmentation [ˌfræɡmen’teɪʃn]

例句 • However, the major problems of the travel and tourism industry that have hidden, or obscured, its economic impact are the diversity and fragmentation of the industry itself. (IELTS10,T3,R1然而 ，旅游业的主要问题在于它本身具有多样性和碎片化的特征 ，这使得它对经济的影响呈现隐性或模糊性 。

fraught [frɔːt]

释义 • adj. with sth. filled with sth.; charged with sth. 充满的 ；worried or anxious; worrying 烦恼的，担心的，令人忧虑的；难以应付的

搭配 • be fraught with sth. 充满某事物

例句 • But translating corporate philosophies into the right mix of colour, style, degree of branding and uniformity can be a fraught process. (IELTS3,TB,R3) 把公司理念转化为颜色 、风格 、品牌和一致性的综合体是一个非常复杂的过程 。

freeway [’friːweɪ]

friction [’frɪkʃən]

释义 • n. the rubbing of one object or surface against another 摩擦，摩擦力 ；conflict, as between persons having dissimilar ideas or interests; clash 矛盾

联想 • 润滑油的作用 (function)是减少摩擦力 (friction)

派生 • frictive adj. 摩擦性的

例句 • Goods, once they have been made, are assumed to move instantly and at no cost from place to place. The real world, however, is full of frictions . (IELTS6,T1,R2) 货物一旦被制造出来 ，人们就假设它无成本地从一个地方流通到另一个地方 。但是在真实的情况下却充满了阻力 。

fringe [frɪndʒ]

释义 • n. the front hair cut so that it hangs over the forehead 刘海，流苏 ；a decorative border or edging of hanging threads, cords, or strips, often attached to a separate band 穗子 ；a marginal, peripheral, or secondary part 边缘，外围 v. to have sth. as a border 饰……的边，以……为界

搭配 • the lunatic fringe 极端分子

例句 • Further more,they thought that only a lunatic fringe of about one in 1,000 would give the highest shock of 450 volts. (IELTS5,T1,R2) 另外 ，他们认为大约千分之一的狂热分子会施以 450伏的电击 。

frost [frɒst]

释义 • n. the dew or water vapour frozen into tiny white ice crystals that cover the ground, etc. when the temperature falls below freezing-point 霜，霜冻 ；a weather condition in which the temperature falls below freezing-point, usu. accompanied by the formation of fros 冰冻，严寒 v. to cover (sth.) with frost 使结霜，下霜

派生 • frost-bound adj. 冻结的

frosting n. (撒在蛋糕上的 )糖霜

例句 • Thousands starved as the harvests failed, after snow in June and frosts in August. (IELTS4,T3,R2) 6月暴雪和 8月霜冻使庄稼歉收 ，成千上万的人挨饿 。

froth [frɒθ]

释义 • n. a mass of small bubbles, esp. on the surface of a liquid; foam (液体表面的)泡，泡沫 ；a light but worthless conversation, ideas, etc. 空谈，浅薄的想法 v. to cause (a liquid) to foam 起泡沫，冒泡

例句 • The gases trapped inside the boiling rock expand suddenly, the lava glows with heat, it begins to froth , and it explodes with tremendous force. (IELTS4,T3,R2) 困在沸石中的气体突然膨胀 ，岩浆受热发红 ，开始起泡 ，然后爆炸 ，释放出很大的能量 。

frown [fraʊn]

搭配 • frown at对 ……皱眉

frown upon/on 反对 ，不喜欢

例句 • These and other perquisites of status are often frowned upon, but they may serve a purpose as a kind of uniform in a democratic society; roles without signs often lead to confused or differing expectations of the role of the focal person. (IELTS3,T2,R3) 这些以及其他一些表示社会地位的特权经常让人感到反感 ，但作为民主社会的一种标志 ，它们还是有作用的 ；没有标记的角色常常导致对焦点人物的期待值趋于混乱或不一致 。

fruitful [’fruːtfəl]

fume [fjuːm]

fuzzy [ˈfʌzi]

gauge [geɪdʒ]

例句 • It gauges the pollution from a passing vehicle—more useful than the annual stationary test that is the British standard today—by bouncing a beam through the exhaust and measuring what gets blocked. (IELTS3,T4,R1) 它对行驶中的汽车的尾气发出光束 ，并通过测量被阻拦的物质来确定污染程度 ，这种方法比英国现在标准的每年一次的固定测试的方法更有效 。

generalisation [ˌdʒenərəlɑɪ’zeɪʃən]

gimmick [’gɪmɪk]

glacial [’ɡleɪʃəl]

gloomy [’ɡluːmɪ]

gorgeous [’ɡɔːdʒəs]

gossip [’ɡɒsɪp]

grease [griːs]

grim [grɪm]

释义 • adj. very bad or unpleasant 讨厌的，糟糕的 ；very serious and unsmiling in appearance 严肃的，严厉的 ；severe; unrelenting 严酷的，无情的
